B0083P1QUM|1.0|I downloaded \\"The Bone Bed\\" because I recalled reading an early Cornwell offering in the past and thought she might put together an entertaining page turner. My memory didn't serve me well. Cornwell has some issues that she needs to work out on the psychiatrist's couch instead of throwing them at her readers.<br /><br />Her characters have all of the subtlety of Macy's Thanksgiving Parade floats; her protagonist Kay Scarpetta is not only a Medical Examiner, but an attorney and an Army Major who never served in combat. Scarpetta's lesbian niece Lucy is some sort of uber-genius computer hacker, renegade FBI investigator and daredevil helicopter pilot. It's a slicer! A dicer! It even makes Julienne fries! Much like the late night product info-mercials, her female characters can do everything except have flaws like normal mortals.<br /><br />The flaws all pile up on the male sub-characters; Pete Marino is a drunken loudmouth and socially incompetent detective who almost sleeps at Scarpetta's feet at the morgue. Her husband Benton is a one-dimensional shadow figure, dragged out to give Scarpetta someone to talk at. Other male characters want to bed Scarpetta because she's not only attractive, but it would be a professional accomplishment for them to be granted the privilege.<br /><br />The plot is a mishmash of a leatherback turtle, a mummified woman and a severed ear. Good ingredients that never come together in a satisfying main course. If a Stephen King book is a bloody steak with all the trimmings and a Lee Child novel is a hoagie sandwich grabbed while running from bad guys through a foreign airport, then \\"The Bone Bed\\" by Patricia Cornwell is a water cracker, a sprig of parsley and an old dinner mint found between your car seats.<br /><br />Oh, \\"misandry\\" is a word that doesn't come up much. It's the opposite of \\"misogyny\\".

B003OF3R0S|4.0|Following the sudden death of original drummer/co-founder James \\"The Rev\\" Sullivan in December of 2009, Avenged Sevenfold were broken-hearted but not discouraged. They soon recruited an even better drummer -- a guy named Mike Portnoy from Dream Theater -- and hurried into the studio to record their fifth album, 2010's \\"Nightmare.\\"<br /><br />A7X definitely wear their influences -- which range from Metallica and Pantera to Queensryche and Judas Priest -- on their sleeves this time around. But nevertheless, they definitely still have some sizeable musical chops and instrumental prowess. And \\"Nightmare\\" also proves that the band's songwriting talents have also improved greatly over the years (they debuted with \\"Sounding The Seventh Trumpet\\" in 2001). They concoct both hard-hitting, mosh-pit-friendly metallic hard rockers and docile, laid back ballads equally as well. For the most part, though, this is a traditional heavy metal/metallic hard rock record, and one that is streaked with thrash, power, and progressive metal influences. (And only occasionally does it dive back into the metalcore sound of old.)<br /><br />The title song begins with a quiet, minor-key intro before Portnoy's explosive, driving double bass drums come thundering in. This is then followed by fiery, crunchy, chugging riffs and some irresistibly nasal-sounding vocal hooks (including a catchy, if very clich&eacute; and Alice Cooper-esque chorus: \\"I am your effing nightmare!\\"). A lengthy, winding, dive-bombing guitar solo is included in this strong set opener, too, and a cool piano speckles its outro. The album then takes a turn towards the metalcore days of old with \\"Welcome To The Family,\\" a clear-cut choice for being the lead-single. It features a deft drum intro, insanely catchy vocal hooks, fist-pumping choruses, Iron Maiden-inspired dual guitar harmonies, and double bass-aided breakdowns. \\"Danger Line\\" has a rhythmic, martial drum beat and some soaring, piercing guitar harmonies in its intro. From there, it soon adopts some thrashy, chugging riffs, and soaring, winding, classical-metal-sounding harmonies. This then flows into a bit of clean crooning, thought-provoking lyrics, and a somber keyboard solo that, subsequently, flows into a winding melodic solo to end.<br /><br />\\"Buried Alive,\\" with its slow, melodic intro that leads into a strong, chugging main riff and chugging breakdowns followed by a part where guitarists Synyster Gates and Zacky Vengeance trade-off exceptional solos, very closely evokes Metallica's \\"One.\\" (But this should be viewed as a nice homage to one of A7X's biggest influences, not as a simple rip-off.) Add some good lyrics to the mix, and the end result is a song that is a hit-single, but a very epic one at that, as it has unorthodox structuring and a nearly seven-minute long playing time. Next up is the blazing, muscularly-riffed \\"Natural Born Killer,\\" which begins with a brutal, blistering bout of buzzsaw-fast thrash picking before segueing into propulsive, fiery chugging and shredding solos. But this is immediately offset by a tear-jerking, Southern rock-flavored ballad named \\"So Far Away,\\" which just might be the album's pinnacle. (It, too, is a hit-single, and rightfully so!) It is highlighted by exceptional, accomplished clean singing and excellent -- if very depressing -- lyricism. (Its subject matter doesn't directly pertain to The Rev's passing; but -- with lines like \\"Another chapter laid to rest\\" and \\"How do I live without the ones I love?\\" -- it might as well have.) It also features some bluesy melodic soloing, and anthemic, lighter-waving choruses.<br /><br />Then comes another surprisingly heavy and thrashy piece of metalcore called \\"God Hates Us,\\" which is fueled by brisk speed metal riffing, bullying double bass drumming, and a Kirk Hammett-esque solo. Then it's right back to the balladry, though, as the proceeding \\"Victim\\" is another sprawling, Queensryche-ian power ballad that clocks in at seven-and-a-half minutesin length and has huge, infectious choruses. And then there's \\"Tonight The World Dies,\\" which is another ballad with Southern, Lynnyrd Skynnyrd-inspired bluesy melodic leads and acoustic strumming. Unfortunately, after that, \\"Nightmare\\" begins to stumble a little bit. \\"Fiction\\" isn't a bad song by any means, but it should be chalked-up as a misstep on account of being one-too-many a ballad in a row. (Three is kind of a lot.) As a result of this, as well as the use of some so-so (and ever-so syrupy) clean vocals and corny vibes, \\"Fiction\\" is a thoroughly mediocre track, and one that does not add much other than a cool piano line and some nearly-symphonic-sounding synths. But all is well that ends well, and \\"Nightmare\\" ends very well. At eleven-whole minutes in length, \\"Save Me\\" might overstay its welcome, but it is nonetheless a strong set closer, and one that is driven by thunderous double bass and blast beats. It also boasts some faint, haunting orchestral touches, fiery, sinewy, winding guitar leads/solos, and heavy, bruising breakdowns.<br /><br />While not album-of-the-year-worthy, or even a career-defining watershed release (this reviewer is still partial to Avenged Sevenfold's 2003 effort, \\"Waking The Fallen\\"), \\"Nightmare\\" is a very accomplished, well-written, well-rounded, and impeccably-played affair. All of which make it a worthy follow-up to A7X's self-titled 2007 release, and a very solid effort, overall. And had \\"Fiction\\" been scrapped from the record (which it definitely should have been), I probably would have given it a five-star rating.gth and has huge, infectious choruses. B000O178BY|5.0|Trent Reznor's Nine Inch Nails returned after a six-year hiatus in 2005, with that year's \\"With Teeth.\\" But even if this reviewer was slightly disappointed by that release, he needn't fret about it too much, because Trent's creativity cycle was only just beginning. As such, NIN returned only two years later with a wildly epic and commanding new record called \\"Year Zero.\\"<br /><br />This album has been getting most of its much-buzzed about press from a lyrical standpoint, as it is a concept album detailing the singer's predictions of how this war-torn world will lead to an eventual apocalypse and destruction of mankind. This is new ground for Reznor, who usually spends most of his time on Nine Inch Nails albums attacking organized religion, and encouraging atheism. It is a great, and undeniably scary story he tells, here - and part of what is so frightening about it is that his predictions are all very believable and even distinctly possible. But the record is also of note on a musical standpoint. Trent crafts together sixteen carefully-calculated tunes, here, and they are all comprised of darkly catchy, and often indescribable sonic soundscapes. The end result frequently is a bunch of songs that sound quite danceable, and are always very memorable. They are loaded with NIN's signature heavy bass lines, computer-gone-haywire-esque sound effects, and classically techno-industrial-derived clicks, beeps, cyber-smash, and Ministry-like meticulous, stomping rhythms and ominous vocals.<br /><br />\\"Year Zero\\" opens with \\"Hyperpower!,\\" a very cool, instrumental track consisting of a dexterous, reverberating drum solo from Josh Freeze (of A Perfect Circle fame). Track two (\\"The Beginning Of The End\\") is a terrifically catchy number with rhythmic, staccato beat and memorable lyrics (\\"We think we've climbed so high/Up all the backs we've condemned/This is the beginning of the end,\\" etc.). Two other, obvious highlights of the album's first half are the two lead singles, \\"Survivalism\\" (and \\"Capital G.\\" The latter of these two, with its hooky, staccato beat and vocals, is quite possibly the catchiest thing Trent has ever recorded. It also features really great choruses, as well as some of the album's most straight-forward and memorable lyrics (i.e. \\"I pushed the button and elected him to office/He pushed the button and dropped the bomb.\\") Another is the dance-floor-ready rhythms and memorable, electronic-tinged vocals of the indescribable soundscape that is \\"Vessel.\\" And \\"My Violent Heart,\\" which trades-off spoken word narration (with more noteworthy lyricism) in the verses with climactic, powerful choruses, is another.<br /><br />Working your way through the second half of the album, there are bass-driven numbers like \\"The Warning\\" and \\"Meet Your Master.\\" \\"The Greater Good\\" is also a bass-heavy piece (it is propelled by a huge, fuzzy-sounding electronic bass line); but it also features a simplistic, rock `n' roll-esque drum beat, catchy, repetitive rhythms, and a nice, sweeping piano line. This is a mostly-instrumental track, although it does have some faint and bone-chilling whispers in the background. Other highlights of the second half include the distinctly, very Skinny Puppy-esque \\"The Great Destroyer\\" (which boasts accomplished clean singing) and \\"In This Twilight\\"; and \\"Another Version Of The Truth,\\" which, essentially, plays like a continuation of the 1994 NIN classic \\"Hurt.\\"<br /><br />If you are looking for a slab of heavy industrial metal, you will be sorely disappointed with \\"Year Zero.\\" But if it is richly textured, epic, commanding, encompassing industrial metal that you crave, the album will yield some richly rewarding listening sessions. Let's just hope Trent's bleak world view and predictions about the future remain safely, firmly in his own head.lism\\" (and \\"Capital G.\\" The latter of these two, with its hooky, staccato beat and vocals, is quite possibly the catchiest thing Trent has ever recorded. It's the perfect film for such a monumental anniversary.<br /><br />Without getting too spoilery, \\"Skyfall\\" has Bond resurrecting himself after a slam bang pre-credits sequence that finds 007's life up in the air. He reports back to duty when someone has attacked MI6. It seems someone has a top secret list that exposes the identities of agents out in the field, and it's someone who hits close to home with M (the amazing Dame Judi Dench).<br /><br />Like many people my age, my introduction to Bond was Roger Moore. That's who I grew up with at first, but got to see Connery on TV and video. Connery was the best (and I have a soft spot for Pierce Brosnan as well), but it took me a while to warm up to Daniel Craig. 'Casino Royale' was a fine film and 'Quantum Of Solace' was a disaster. 'Skyfall' is Craig's third Bond film, but it's the first where it feels like he is finally a Bond that I can warm up to and put him right alongside the others. It's a movie that breaks the mold with 007, but also retains the classic elements of the franchise. It's also those classic moments that had the audience I saw with applauding the most. The classics never go out of style.<br /><br />I cannot stress enough how amazing the movie looks. Cinematograpger Roger Deakins has created the best looking Bond I have ever seen. Truly a memorable presence. Ralph Fiennes, Naomie Harris and Albert Finney are also new to the game. We finally get a new Q as well, in the guide of a young computer geek played by Ben Wishaw. And Daniel Craig. He is finally James Bond in this one. Definitely his best. He makes Bond human and vulnerable like never before.<br /><br />\\"Skyfall\\" explores more about Bond's past than we have ever seen in a 007 movie. It does a good job of new revelations in a new age, but also keeps those classic hallmarks that we have all come to know and love in the series. You can't have Bond without them. \\"Skyfall\\" is exceptionally directed by Sam Mednes, who delivers not only one of the best Bond films, but one of the best action films I have seen in years. The stunts are magnificent, the action is breathtaking, the cinematography is beautiful, the music is amazing. \\"Skyfall\\" is Bond at his best.

B008BO61BE|5.0|\\"Screaming For Vengeance,\\" the sixth album proper from the almighty English heavy metal quintet Judas Priest, is a resounding success. Although not quite as amazing as 1980's watershed release \\"British Steel,\\" it is still a timeless classic. It is also one of the most influential records of the 1980's, as it would prove to go on to inspire an unquantifiable number of power metal, progressive metal, and thrash/speed metal bands.<br /><br />\\"S.F.V.\\" is full of the heavy metal good stuff. What this means is expect tons of stellar, passionate vocals from frontman Rob Halford, a tight rhythm section -- comprised of Dave Holland's deft, natural-sounding drumming and Ian Hill's steady bass bottom -- and, most importantly, great riffs and even greater solos from axe-duo-extraordinaire Glenn Tipton and K.K. Downing.<br /><br />The record blasts off with \\"The Hellion,\\" an early piece of thrash/speed metal. It is a lightning-fast blitzkrieg of speed punk-ish drumming (including an eight-second long, bouncy, crashing drum solo in the intro), propulsive speed metal riffs, grumbling bass notes, and catchy and commanding vocals. A fist-pumping chorus is also included, and the opener is capped off by both a soaring, several-parted melodic solo and some neat twin-guitar harmonies. \\"Electric Eye, \\"with its hooky, single-note, riff, crashing drum beat, galloping, head-bobbing rhythm, is quite possibly the catchiest song found anywhere on here. And a ripping, classical-sounding guitar solo is also included. \\"Riding On The Wind\\" is another insanely rhythmic head-banger backed by industrial-strength, churning guitar leads, punchy, dexterous drumming, and strong, humming bass line. (And dig the tune's choral interludes, too.)<br /><br />\\"Bloodstone\\"'s crunchy, fiery, machine-gun guitar licks (that come cascading down on the listener's eardrums), galloping, chugging bass line, and soulful, melodic singing make it another standout. It also has a bouncy drum beat that fills any leftover space perfectly well, and, like the riffage, some similarly fiery melodic soloing to end. \\"(Take These) Chains\\" marries a cool, futuristic-sounding intro with strong, propulsive, staccato guitar hooks, and a steady, humming bass bottom. And its chant-worthy sing-along vocals and huge, concert-ready choruses serve as just the icing on the cake. \\"Pain And Pleasure\\" has stellar, power metal-esque vocals (that practically scream \\"classic Halford!\\"), and muscular, churning rhythms. But for the most part, though, this is a bass-driven song; as it features some very interesting and noteworthy bass work throughout. (This includes a funky-sounding bottom-end and some meaty, heavy bass throbs.)<br /><br />The title track may have catchy, shouted vocals, but it is the guitarists that take over the spotlight, here. And they do so with crunching riffs and epic, instinctively memorable, and pyrotechnic soloing. \\"You've Got Another Thing Comin',\\" however, is highlighted by what is perhaps \\"S.F.V.\\"'s best solo -- and what a lengthy, mazy, complex, multi-parted, soulfully emphatic, and wailing solo it is, too. It is classic Judas Priest, through and through. \\"You've Got...,\\" which is a semi-power ballad, is also highlighted by dreamy acoustic guitar melodies, crunchy electric guitars, and piercingly falsetto and harmonic, glass-shattering vocals. And another solo -- this one is of the more blistering, shredding, and wah-drenched variety -- comes ripping through the mix, too.<br /><br />\\"Feber\\" is another cut of early speed metal, as it is a propulsive, lean and mean number with a memorable, pounding main riff, chug and churning rhythms, an adherent, mosh pit-ready groove, and another unorthodox, shredding, whammy bar solo. \\"Devil's Child\\" (which is the proper end of the album) lays gentle acoustic strums and atmospheric keyboards against thudding, throbbing rhythms, thus creating a new-wavy, and borderline -creepy vibe. Some deliciously melodic leads and an acoustic guitar solo help this cause, though, too. Finally, the set wraps up with a bunch of flawlessly-executed live renditions of various songs -- most of which were recorded live at the San Antonio civic center in September of 1982. And a b-side from the 1985 \\"Turbo\\" recording sessions (\\"Prisoner Of Your Eyes\\") is also included as a bonus track.<br /><br />One of the Priest's greatest achievements.s cause, though, too. B00005UEAR|5.0|The sixth full-length album from New York-based prog metal godfathers/innovators Dream Theater, 2002's \\"Six Degrees Of Inner Turbulence,\\" is perhaps the band's most epic release of their storied, influential career. While not as essential as, say, 1992's \\"Images And Words,\\" it is still yet another fine record from D.T.. Comprised of two different discs, \\"Six Degrees\\" sounds like it was made by a bunch of people with bipolar disorder, as it explores both soft, experimental and metallic, hard-hitting territory. It is a conceptual piece, detailing the lives of six individuals suffering from bipolarity, post-traumatic stress, schizophrenia, post-partum depression, autism, and dissociative personality disorder.<br /><br />But \\"Six Degrees\\" is also of note from a musical standpoint -- of course. Guitar god John Petrucci's fretwork is always highly technical and impressive. The drumming of Mike Portnoy, and bass work of John Myung are very good, too, and keyboardist Jordan Rudess is prominently audible in the mix, as well. But for the most part, the music is focused around said axeman --and dang, is it ever great! And instinctively memorable, too. He lays down piles of riffs -- and whether aggressive and heavy or progg-y and melodic, they are always very inventive, technically-proficient, and interesting. And his solos -- my god, his solos! He augments his riffing with mile after mile of equally amazing and wailing solos.<br /><br />Disc one is made up of almost entirely made-up of experimental songs. Almost. The big exception to that is the high-octane opener \\"The Glass Prison,\\" which has three different parts to it: \\"Reflection,\\" \\"Restoration,\\" and \\"Revelation.\\" After an acoustic intro, the dramatic electric guitars come storming onto the scene, with catchy, Dimebag Darrell-esque wah-wah guitar licks backed by mean, driving double bass drumming. And it all forms a crunchy, staccato, head-bangable groove that the song adheres to for the duration of its thirteen-minute playing time. Some very progressive, technical, and sweeping melodic guitar soloing is also included in this powerful set opener, as is a technical, slapped, walking bass solo. And it all wraps up with an excellent, epic, dual-guitar soloing section, with one ripping, whammy-bar-laden solo, and one screaming and winding solo. The ten-and-a-half minute-long \\"Blind Faith\\" brings back some of those impressive soloing skills found in the first track, as Petrucci lays down some great, Slash-esque solo flights. But the song is also highlighted by a flowing melodic bass groove, docile melodic vocals, and a very tricky keyboard solo.<br /><br />\\"Misunderstood\\" might gain momentum and heaviness off of itself, morphing into a thundering bass groove and technical, shredding soloing. But for the most part, though, this is a very dreamy and heavenly, Radiohead-esque synth-driven ballad. (Dig that proggy synth soloing, throughout!) Next, the politically-charged \\"The Great Debate\\" draws influence mostly from Tool and A Perfect Circle. Its James Maynard Keenan-esque vocals really drive-home the track's noteworthy political lyrics; and there are also numerous politically-based samples that are about stem cell research. But \\"Great Debate\\" is also of note on a musical level, too; as it features an excellent, ominous bass intro, proggy, jazzy drumming, keyboard-sounding guitar leads, and another stellar, screaming, wailing melodic solo. The first disc wraps up with \\"Disappear,\\" a very pretty and somber acoustic guitar/synthesizer-driven ballad.<br /><br />The second disc is comprised of one song with six-different parts. Kicking off the second disc is \\"Overture,\\" which fuses in a full orchestra into its mix, thus making this a rich-sounding instrumental opener, and one that is full of gorgeous textures layered on top of each other. \\"About To Crash\\" picks up right where \\"Overture\\" leaves off, augmenting a melodic string arrangement with sweeping, symphonic-sounding piano and keyboard runs.Then, following \\"War Inside My Head\\" (which is seemingly out of place, clocking in at just over two minutes in length), comes \\"The Test That Stumped Them All,\\" which, with its crunching grooves, staccato, chugging riffs, and thundering drum fills, almost plays like a sequel to Pantera's \\"By Demons Be Driven.\\" Other highlights of the second disc include \\"Goodnight Kiss,\\" which opens with dreamy acoustic plucking and has a wealth of wailing keyboard runs, really epic and jazzy guitar soloing, and rhythmically staccato, chunky, beeping bass lines; and the nicely melodic bass work, sweeping, symphonic-sounding keyboards, and insanely tricky and technical acoustic guitar work in the power ballad \\"Solitary Shell.\\"<br /><br />Again, \\"Six Degrees\\" is not Dream Theater's magnum-opus, but it is good enough to warrant being a standout in the band's discography. It is as excellent and rewarding as it is unpredictable, making it one of the best metal releases of 2002, and also one of the best progressive metal albums of the new millennium.Then, following \\"War Inside My Head\\" (which is seemingly out of place, clocking in at just over two minutes in length), comes \\"The Test That Stumped Them All,\\" which, with its crunching grooves, staccato, chugging riffs, and thundering drum fills, almost plays like a sequel to Pantera's \\"By Demons Be Driven.\\" Other highlights of the second disc include \\"Goodnight Kiss,\\" which opens with dreamy acoustic plucking and has a wealth of wailing keyboard runs, really epic and jazzy guitar soloing, and rhythmically staccato, chunky, beeping bass lines; and the nicely melodic bass work, sweeping, symphonic-sounding keyboards, and insanely tricky and technical acoustic guitar work in the power ballad \\"Solitary Shell.\\"<br /><br />Again, \\"Six Degrees\\" is not Dream Theater's magnum-opus, but it is good enough to warrant being a standout in the band's discography. Mendez poses as a Canadian producer scouting exotic location for a Hollywood sci-fi film \\"Argo\\" - a film project that does not exist. And he disguises the trapped American embassy workers as Canadian film crew members so that they can get out of Iran safely. This is his \\"best bad idea\\" - but will that \\"bad idea\\" really work?<br /><br />Set in the middle of the Iranian Revolution (of which background is briefly shown in the opening), \\"Argo\\" is a tense and fast-paced thriller that never lets up. Believe me or not, the film is also funny at times.<br /><br />Like most films \\"based on true events,\\" \\"Argo\\" sometimes seems taking liberties with the facts, especially in its second half. B000002ITW|3.0|Growing up in the mid 70's, Crosby Stills Nash (& Young) were my favorite group. The debut Crosby Stills & Nash album, & Deja Vu, were the two most influential albums on me.<br />This one, too, evokes strong memories... but unfortunately, not all positive. There are some great moments here, but there are at least as many major critiques as there are positive things to say about this album.<br />Let's begin with the good. Young, in particular, sparkles. If you were to list the best tracks of this disk, at least 5 of the top 6 would have to be Neil's. From the opening chords of \\"On the Way Home,\\" to the dramatic \\"Ohio\\" (written within days of the Kent State shootings, & performed here only weeks later), Young far outshines his colleagues. Cowgirl in the Sand takes on a haunting quality. Southern Man goes on too long (Young introduces the song by saying \\"this is a really long song, & tonight we are going to play it real slow\\"), but is outstanding. & then there is \\"Ohio,\\" a song that no one over the 10 when it came out can ever forget. The addition of the Loner/Cinnamon Girl/Down by the River medley is by far the best of the bonus tracks.<br />The acoutstic side has a few other nice moments. I have always been a sucker for Crosby's rich voice, and it is on full display in Lee Shore & Triad (even if some of his harmonies with his long time partner Nash are a bit rough on Lee Shore). His Long Time Coming is some great 60's paranoia, well played here.<br />The additions of Black Queen, King Midas in Reverse, and Laughing add some value, but are not particularly notable.<br />For the most part, the acoustic side is comprised of 4 solo artists taking turns. There are a few decent collaborations, but there are at least as many screwups. You can applaud the original producers of the record for leaving Crosby & Nash's false start on \\"Right Between the Eyes\\" for their unflinching honesty, or their attempt to bring a little levity to the proceedings, but frankly these guys oughtto be embarrassed. Most likely, they were so completely high, they screwed up.<br />More negatives:<br />* Nash sounds downright shrill throughout. None of his pieces work. Pre Road Downs in particular is just terrible.<br />* Stills' contrributions are weak as well.<br />* Carry On and Pre Road Downs are simply unlistenable. At least the latter is short: Carry On, perhaps CSNY's 2nd best song (after Suite) might be the worst 14 minutes or so ever recorded. The \\"jam\\" is just terrible.<br />* Why the heck didn't they clean up the recording quality with the release of the CD? Surely something could have been done to improve the just awful sound quality.<br />* Suite Judy Blue Eyes: I still kind of have a soft spot in my heart for the way they sort of seque into the album with just about 30 seconds of Suite Judy Blue Eyes. But especially on re-release, with bonus tracks, why not give us a decent version of CSN's quintessential song? Nash later admitted this was a \\"mistake\\". Why not rectify it now? Eg, drop the OK but completely unnecessary \\"Black Queen\\" (which clocks in at nearly 7 minutes, more than enough time) and replace it with Suite Judy Blue Eyes? Even keeping the opening 30 second intro?<br />Lets finish as the album finishes, with Find the Cost of Freedom. Crosby quiets the crowd, saying \\"this is wooden music now, you've got to be quiet, or else you won't hear it.\\" The song has a hushed quality that lends gravitas to the performance. Even if not every harmony is spot on, the whole of it is far greater than the sum of its parts.<br />I will forever be 16 years old when I listen to this disk. It takes me back to another place in time, and evokes a lot of happy memories for me. I suspect the same will be true for a number of folks in their 50s & 60s. Most people have already decided long ago about this disk. For those handful of folks out there who remained on the fence, go ahead & take the plunge. Yeah, its got warts. So do a lot of folks our age.

B00942S4OY|4.0|One Direction follow-up 2012's smash debut [[ASIN:B006ZZAMWK Up All Night]] with a quick follow-up via fall 2012's [[ASIN:B00942S4OY Take Me Home]].  Take Me Home ends up being a more well-rounded effort than the band's debut, exhibiting growth from every member. That doesn't signify the band still doesn't possess a personality problem as far as transference to an album, but the voices are more distinct of one another this time. Essentially, Take Me Home adequately satisfies its niche - teen-pop/pop.<br /><br />\\"Live While We're Young\\" unsurprisingly kicks off Take Me Home keeping in mind the sensibilities of previous smash \\"What Makes You Beautiful.\\"  Liam opens the cut vocally while Zayn ends up getting the meatiest parts. The chorus is equally addictive and schmaltzy (\\"Let's go crazy, crazy, crazy 'til we see the sun...tonight let's get some, and live while we're young\\"), but accomplishes its feat.<br /><br />\\"Kiss You\\" outperforms \\"Live While We're Young,\\" characterized by quick tempo and quick-paced vocals. The chorus is nothing short of pop gold: \\"So tell me girl if every time we touch/you get this kind of rush/baby say yeah yeah yeah.\\" Add some obligatory corniness via \\"na na na na...\\" and \\"Kiss You\\" will easily get stuck in anyone's head.<br /><br />\\"Little Things,\\" penned by singer/songwriter Ed Sheeran (and Fiona Bevan), showcases One Direction's most mature song to date, sporting a slower pace. The thoughtful songwriting leads this mature charge, but the boys deliver, particularly the chorus:\\"I won't let these little things/slip out of my mouth/but if I do/it's you, it's you they add up to/I'm in love with you/and all these little things...\\" Another selling point is that each member has a distinct solo here. There is little quibble, though the cut does `sit' a bit with its acoustic guitar production stylings.<br /><br />\\"C'mon, C'mon\\" speeds things back up with an 80s influenced chorus. It lacks the magic of \\"Kiss You\\" but remains a solid entity. \\"Last First Kiss\\" is better, opting for a mid-tempo groove.  Production work is solid, with drums and guitars sounding particularly excellent within the mix.  The chorus is predictably humongous, but that is a good thing (\\"I wanna be last, yeah/baby let me be oh let me be your last first kiss...\\") One of the album's finest.<br /><br />\\"Heart Attack\\" has a funky-pop groove and is gimmicky without overreaching. It is schmaltz-laden, given the notion that love can give you a heart attack, but this is teen-pop after all.<br />Dr. Luke is among the producers on the Queen-influenced \\"Rock Me.\\" The production borrows cues from \\"We Will Rock You,\\" attuning that sensibility to One Direction. The chorus is a selling point as always, especially the melodic pattern on lyrics \\"...I want you to hit the pedal heavy metal, show me you care...\\" Louis gets some much needed vocal love, delivering a catchy pre-chorus (\\" I used to think that I was better alone/why did I ever wanna let you go...\\"). Repetitiveness and perhaps over simplicity are the only rub.<br /><br />\\"Change My Mind\\" is one of the albums weaker cuts. It is by no means horrible, but lacks the oomph of the best. \\"I Would\\" easily atones, characterized by slick production work. The chorus is irresistible: \\"Would he say that he's in L-O-V-E? Well if it was me, I would (I would)/would he hold you when you're feeling low? Baby you should know that I would (I would)...\\" \\"I Would\\" is undeniably satisfying.<br /><br />\\"Over Again\\" is the second Ed Sheeran co-write, laden with ultra rhythmic lyrics. It is not bad, though some may prefer \\"Little Things.\\" \\"Back For You\\" is stronger, sporting catchy chorus and slick production. \\"Back For You\\" is amongst the top tier. Penultimate cut \\"They Don't Know About Us\\" is an urban-pop cut; truly the only one of its kind on Take Me Home. A solid change of pace, this cut is appropriately placed near the end. \\"Summer Love\\" closes. It gives Irish member Niall Horan his largest role as of yet, handlingthe chorus upon its first iteration (\\"cause you were mine for the summer/now we know it's nearly over/feels like snow in September...\\").  Overall, it solid, though not the `cream of the crop.'<br /><br />Overall, [[ASIN:B00942S4OY Take Me Home]] is a solid pop album. Yes it is corny and at times incredibly schmaltzy, but it appeals and plays to it's base exceptionally.  There are no overt misses - even \\"Change My Mind\\" works well enough - which makes this album more appealing than their platinum debut. What the band does need to keep working on is developing more personality. The voices are becoming more distinct, but this needs to continue in order to make One Direction transcend being a pop trend.the chorus upon its first iteration (\\"cause you were mine for the summer/now we know it's nearly over/feels like snow in September...\\").  Overall, it solid, though not the `cream of the crop.'<br /><br />Overall, [[ASIN:B00942S4OY Take Me Home]] is a solid pop album. Yes it is corny and at times incredibly schmaltzy, but it appeals and plays to it's base exceptionally.  There are no overt misses - even \\"Change My Mind\\" works well enough - which makes this album more appealing than their platinum debut. What the band does need to keep working on is developing more personality. The voices are becoming more distinct, but this needs to continue in order to make One Direction transcend being a pop trend.

It also has tremendous control over world trade and media as a result of which millions of people around the world get a glimpse of life in America even if they have never crossed the border of their own cities/towns/villages. People - particularly from developing countries - want to be in America in order to make it big and lead comfortable lives.<br />It is therefore quite surprising that there is considerable resentment among people around the world towards America. It, in many cases, originates from radical ideas. Traditionally, the adopters of these radical ideas are found in religious schools (madrassas) in poor regions around the world.<br />But, in the last few years, this ideology has not left unscathed even the educated elite in the developed world( Amhad Omar Sheikh being a pretty good example).<br /><br />The book does not investigate topics like terrorism/wars/religion...etc. Infact, there are no terrorists in the book at all.<br />However, it does make an attempt to delve deeply into how events (like 9/11) tend to impact our thought process. This process changes normal people leading normal lives into fundamentalists. And sometimes, it also makes people deeply and unreasonably suspicious of people from other ethnicities.<br /><br />The leading protagonist(Changez) is a young man who has come to America with ambitions not unlike many other South Asians. He belongs to a family that is well-respected in Lahore. However, because of the political and economic situation in Pakistan, their wealth and position has been in constant decline over the years.<br />Changez, not lacking ambition, completes his studies with zeal and gets the job of his dreams.<br /><br />Belonging to a family that has lost its wealth, but not position in society, he is a proud man and does not want to be looked down upon by his peers.<br />Therefore, while in college, he constructs a false facade of being rich by hiding the fact that he has to work extra jobs in order to make ends meet.<br />He even uses an advance salary from him new job to pay for his vacation in Greece with other Princetonians.<br />When encountered by an elderly doorman during a visit to his girlfriend's (Erica) house who looked disapprovingly at his ethnic attire, he speaks to him haughtily to put him back at his place. Though, according to his own admissions, his country has had little achievements in modern times, he takes a great deal of pride in his ancestry and the historical accomplishments of his country. Perhaps, for this reason, it hurts him a lot when people mention the economic and social problems that plague Pakistan.<br /><br />While in new York, Changez is exceedingly successful professionally and also finds an undestanding mentor in Jim and a good friend in Wainwright. He is often viewed with suspicion.<br />Changez, because of these events and the turmoil in his relationship with Erica, loses his ability to 'focus on the fundamentals' and begins to interpret events around him with ever-increasing influence of his hatred towards American policies. B008O9V4C2|4.0|I have owned this album since day one and have played it to death. Some of the songs are just classic but, as with some other reviewers, some are just not impressing me. Two songs, Slinky Thing and The New Breed are great songs about an older guy hanging out with, and reflecting on attractions and interactions with younger women. A little like Cousin Dupree in that almost \\"dirty old man\\" groove. Truth is, many older guys still think they are 27 years old when it comes to women and Fagan is the one to latch on to that and sing about it.<br /><br />The three songs I have been skipping over are Memorabilia, Weather In My Head and Out Of The Ghetto. In trying to work out why, I realize it is because of the words and not the music. The music on the whole album is amazing - the instrumentation is great and I am loving the melodica being so upfront and bluesy. To me it is reminiscent of Stevie Wonder's harmonica playing. So it is the lack of poetry that disappoints me on those tracks. \\"You can fix the weather in the world, just like Mr Gore says, but what can be done with the weather in my head?\\" just has none of the hipster vibe I am used to - none of that obscure, abstract imagery that I associate with classic SD and Donald Fagan songs. The Isaac Hayes cover contains a great instrumental take on the song but lines like \\"I took you out of the ghetto but I could not take the ghetto out of you\\" are just instantly dated and corny through overuse. It's like \\"You can take the man out of the country but you can't take the country out of the man\\". We've heard it so many times. It once sounded like it meant something deep but then we realized there was no real insight there and then it became annoying. I cringe.<br /><br />And finally, Memorabilia asks the question \\"Have you seen the memorabilia?\\". It does not matter how many times I hear the question, my answer is always \\"Nope. I haven't seen the memorabilia and now I know I never will.\\" And then it becomes annoying, so can youplease stop asking? You're nagging me now. I am not sure why it niggles at me - there are other famous questioning songs that don't have that effect: Have you Ever Seen The Rain?, Who Knows Where the Time Goes?, Blowing in the Wind (How many roads must a man walk down?).<br /><br />But this is Donald Fagan so I know I must be wrong to feel like this and now I don't skip Memorabilia any more- I ignore the titular question and concentrate on the groove - on everything else that is wonderful in the tune. Weather In My Head I am beginning to listen to again because the backing is so damn good but, so far, I am still not ready for Out of the Ghetto even though I get the irony - that he is singing about a different ghetto than Isaac Hayes. It is a throwback cover version that doesn't seem worth the space on the album.<br /><br />Slinky Thing, I'm Not The Same Without You, The New Breed, Miss Marlene, Good Stuff (my favorite), and Planet D'Rhonda stand alongside anything else ever done by Donald Fagan or Steely Dan as pure jazz-rock diamond classics.

Characters uncover more and more of the truth as time goes on, finally revealing what really happened at the end of the season.  What made this story line a little weak to me was the fact that Paul and Zach seemed fairly one dimensional and boring, and most importantly - no one really seemed to give a damn about Mary Alice's suicide.  If she was truly one of the best friends of these four women, how come everything was back to normal and laughs a week later?<br /><br />The only person who truly seems affected by her death is Susan at times, but even then - not so much.  Such a traumatic shock would surely completely tear these people apart, so I think maybe at least a six month instead of one week jump in time from her suicide would have been more appropriate.  I know it's part of the morbidity and all; people selfishly continuing to lead their pointless lives when their best friend just committed suicide.  But even then, it's a stretch.<br /><br />The supporting characters are also fun, such as the creepy Mrs. Huber.  The story lines also interweave very nicely together, and while a lot of it is obviously very silly, it's nicely done in a satirical fashion and the characters still have depth to them, which makes it more than just some silly, stupid show.<br /><br />One of my main issues with this show as a series is the fact that the women never really seemed to have much of a girl friend connection together, like the girls on Sex and the City did.  They act like BFF, but keep so many secrets from one another and their interactions are sort of of weird and sporadic, that it doesn't really feel right.<br /><br />It also has a Twin Peaks feel to it.  The mystery, the drama, the who killed who; if you loved Twin Peaks you may actually like this, male or female.<br /><br />Unfortunately, there is a MAJOR issue with being a parody of something.  There is a fine line between making fun of something and falling into exactly what you're making fun of when you run out ofideas.  That is exactly what happened to Desperate Housewives.  Well, there were two things.  1) lack of creativity/ideas and forcing super contrived story lines, something that wasn't very common in the first season and 2) Cherry had much less to do with the writing and season two, and when you give up your baby to the other writers to control, things like that happen.  Although he came back in the third season, a lot of the damage was permanently done, and it never truly recovered.<br /><br />Great, interesting first season with unbelievable potential, and then....completely failed after that.  Well, at least this season is still worth watching and rewatching here and there.<br /><br />If you like dark comedy/dramas that are Twin Peaks-esque, check this out.  Don't expect the same quality after this season, however.ideas.  That is exactly what happened to Desperate Housewives. B004SUDQ8Q|4.0|This superlative story takes place in 1931 in Western Australia, during a period of time when half-caste Aboriginal children are forcibly taken from their Aboriginal mothers and then raised in a government issued camp for their \\"own benefit\\". This was done out of concern that a third race would become prevalent and to prevent this, they thought that they could change these half-caste children back to a white Western culture over the transformation of three generations. They forced the western culture along with language, religion, and stopped the attempt to mate with additional aboriginals in order to eventually make this culture non-existent. I was completely oblivious to this policy prior to this movie and was dumbfounded to even find that it was even true and was so up until 1970.<br /><br />In this movie, two sisters, Molly and Daisy along with their cousin Gracie find themselves embarking upon a journey to return home over a thousand miles away by following the \\"rabbit proof fence\\", that is used to contain the rabbits in order to protect the farm land. These three young children were half caste Aborigines and were kidnapped from their Aboriginal mothers and sent to Moore River Native Settlement where they are contained because it is what is thought to be best by the white Western Australian culture surrounding them. These children receive education that is motivated to train them as domestic servants and they are taught to turn them from their Aboriginal culture and become \\"white mannered\\". Even with authorities, headed by Kenneth Branagh, watching the Aboriginal children every minute, the girls Molly, Gracie, and Daisy defy all odds and are able to escape Moore's River. While being tracked, they maintain being one step ahead and find help from a few others along their journey but it's the determination of the girl's that keeps them going. I won't ruin the ending but this movie is a must-see. The authoritative figures, especially Kenneth Branagh, could easily be deemed immoral and evil but realistically their intentions were not to harm but to \\"help\\" these children because they thought what they were doing was good and helpful. This movie was extremely emotional and brought smiles, laughter, and lots of tears. The characters brought this movie to life. I don't think this movie is about racism but about cultures and religions thinking that they are helping others by implementing their ideas when in fact it does more harm than good and who are we to dictate what others believe.

B009YU62H2|4.0|Leading up to King Animal's release, I had worry in the back of my mind this new album simply wouldn't sound like Soundgarden. The crux of the worry was Cornell's work over the past decade. While not \\"bad\\" work (I enjoyed some Audioslave, for instance), it certainly wasn't anything like Soundgarden, who by my (and many others) estimation are the closest thing to Led Zeppelin we've seen in the last 30 years. If this turned into a hybrid of Cornell's mellow, much less \\"moody\\" solo work with the powerful, dynamic and brooding Soundgarden, it just wouldn't taste right.<br /><br />My worries were squashed away with this album. While there is the occasional moment that might remind you of Cornell's solo work (Halfway There comes to mind), this album is thoroughly Soundgarden. Right off the bat, the bridge in intro track and single \\"Been Away Too Long\\" screams classic Soundgarden and SG-era Cornell vocal phrasing. \\"And no one KNOWS me! No one SAVES me!\\" Worse Dreams sounds like it could come right off of Superunkown and nobody would have blinked an eye. Haunting tune with a wicked baseline and dark melody. Kim sounds like he didn't miss a beat, his lead work, eery sound effects, and erratic guitar solos reminding me of yesteryear. Cameron and Shepard pull the chaos together into dynamic grooves (Sheperd in particular seems to have a big impact on this album, his baselines pulling you in and never letting go). Little moments like these put away my worries these guys would sound like some weird abomination of themselves. I feel at home listening to King Animal. With that said, I always shy away from comparing band's work to previous works. I prefer to sit back, absorb, and experience as anew without comparisons. With that mindset, King Animal hit me hard. In a very good way.<br /><br />Personally, I find any criticism of this album pointless. Null and void. This album could have never happened, and I feel completely blessed to have been able to experience this album, especially since they represent themselves well with the new music. Is this Badmotorfinger ala 1991 Soundgarden? No. But you're out of your mind if you expected such a thing. It's 2012, these guys are around 50 years old, were apart more than a dozen years, and have proven by their live performances and now new music: They are still legends. They are still Soundgarden, through and through.<br /><br />King Animal proves these guys are still great. It doesn't tarnish their legend, it simply helps it grow and evolve. I'm going to sit back and enjoy Soundgarden while I have the chance. We've all grown, we've all changed, but that isn't a bad thing. I was heartbroken in 1997, and I feel like a long lost friend has returned from a long absence. Welcome back, Soundgarden. We missed you.

B0041KVW2K|2.0|Like many others, I received a defective box set.<br />All 16 albums had the same problem:<br />  The spindle hole is not centered correctly, causing the tone arm to waver from side to side as it plays.<br />That slight movement creates surface noise you'll hear when beginning the record, and damages the cartridge and needle.<br /><br />Second: Abbey Road would not track at all, the needle simply jumped across the vinyl.<br /><br />I discovered by researching online that US copies of this most important music was done at Rainbo pressing plant.<br />Rainbo has a reputation for inconsistent pressings, and a consistent lack of quality control. They are famous for being budget friendly.<br />Why would Apple spend years working on the digital re-mastering with such great attention to every detail, only to hand that work over to a second rate pressing plant?<br />I am stunned by their decision to save money, and present the public with a grossly sub par product like this.<br />I have returned my set to Amazon for a full refund.<br /><br />Then I looked into a UK set in hope that UK pressings would be better.<br />But after reading reviews on Amazon.UK, I discovered many people having issues with warping of the UK pressings.<br />Also, UK pressings with shipping to the US would cost double the price.<br />Any hopes of this box being added to my collection have been dashed.<br /><br />I share my experience in the hope it may help others with their decision to purchase this set or not.<br />The box set was physically beautiful; the book was stunning and of the highest quality.  Album covers were all glossy and true to the originals.<br />Amazon did a fine job with shipping.<br /><br />For me, the most important part of this set is quality of sound.<br />I believe Apple betrayed themselves and the fans with the choice of going to a budget pressing plant.

Yes, the fast pieces on here were the first songs I listened and loved, but it was Hysteria that made me try the album as a whole.<br /><br />Another thing, explore the B-tracks for this album, it's a shame they couldn't be on it for its direct release.<br /><br />And finally, why are there so many butthurt Radiohead fans here reviewing? Just because I think a Radiohead song and a Muse song sound alike doesn't mean I get all pissed and go write a bad review for a Radiohead album. If you don't like it then don't listen, no one is forcing you to listen to Muse.

B009FBX5M0|4.0|Contrary to a popular rumor, Thomas Newman's score for the latest, and the 50th Anniversary edition of the James Bond franchise, Sam Mendes' \\"Skyfall,\\" is hardly the worst of the enormous musical collection; that dubious achievement still belongs to Eric Serra and \\"Goldeneye\\" (to be followed by the late Marvin Hamlisch, \\"The Spy Who Loved Me,\\" Bill Conti, \\"For Your Eyes Only,\\" and George Martin, \\"Live and Let Die\\").  This does not include commentary on theme songs (a great song doth not a great score make), although the last few have been pretty unremarkable Adele's \\"Skyfall,\\" which does not appear on this soundtrack album, comes closer to a true Bond anthem than we have had in quite some time (The best?  \\"Goldfinger,\\" \\"Live and Let Die,\\" \\"You Only Live Twice,\\" \\"Nobody Does it Better,\\" \\"For Your Eyes Only,\\"  \\"We Have All the Time in the World,\\" and \\"Diamonds Are Forever\\").  To be honest Newman's effort is not up there with John Barry's best (\\"On Her Majesty's Secret Service,\\" \\"Goldfinger,\\" \\"You Only Live Twice,\\" \\"Diamonds Are Forever,\\" \\"From Russia With Love,\\" and \\"Thunderball\\"), but it is a good deal better than \\"Dr. No\\" and some of the work of David Arnold.  It is actually surprisingly good as an album, and works very well with what is on the screen (the real test).  And Barry is not with us anymore, so here we are.  There is no lack of kinetic energy here, and Newman knows when to tone things down for reflective, if not romantic, moments (something he is very well known for and with good reason).  He blends a subtle yet sinister main theme throughout and teases with limited use of the James Bond theme just enough to make sure we know this is a Bond epic except for a couple of key moments (\\"Breadcrumbs\\" among them) when it comes through with certitude. Many of us had our doubts about the choice of Newman, but in the end this is a good effort for a film that is certainly a solid production in almost every way with some great touches at the end.  The fundamental problem in scoring a Bond film is simply that Barry was so damnably good and a hard act to follow by even good composers such as Arnold (\\"Tomorrow Never Dies\\") and now Newman (\\"The Horse Whisperer\\").  The recent tendency to leave the theme song off the soundtrack album is too bad but understood given the complications of modern musical contracts and copyright law, and sadly with some of them there is no great loss anyway. The best news is of course that Bond is back in action, and will return. Solid production values and adequate packaging (should have been better for a 50th Anniversary) by Sony.

Zappa might not have been all that aware of it in that fashion,since not only was he extremely busy producing and arranging one mini musical masterpiece after another for seven or eight following this album nearly nonstop that he likely was under the impression that people just weren't getting the point of his music. The album ends with another blues oriented groove in \\"Stink Foot\\",again with another funk oriented lyric about the phoniness of etiquette.<br /><br />  From the very beginning to the very end Frank Zappa has always lyrically focused on often biting social satire that was surrounded by often incredible new fusions of the different musics presented to Zappa by the talented musicians who played with him. B008I34ZG6|5.0|Frank Zappa stands out in my own mind as being one of those few musicians who,if he doesn't already have one,deserves a musical sub genre named after him much in the same manner as Bo Diddly. He seems to have bought all his influences together into a sound that was unpredictable,cocky,witty,explicit and often downright ingenious all at the same time. Following the breakup of the original lineup of the Mothers Of Invention in the early 70's,Zappa regrouped to record two seminal instrumental releases in utilizing the still relatively new jazz-fusion genre. The music's blend of jazz improvisation through psychedelic era rock was just about the perfect base from which Zappa to continue to perfect his art. Best part was his own musical innovations were already moving in that direction organically anyway. Retaining the talents of Ian and Rush Underwood,Don Sugarcane Harris and of course George Duke,he also bought in talents such as Jean Luc Ponty,Napoleon Murphy Brock and even Tina Turner and the Ikettes on backing vocals for this album to re-create,in new vocal and melodic ways,what he'd achieved with his previous two studio releases.<br /><br />  Starting out this set is \\"Camarillo Brillo\\",the closest thing to a standard issue California 70's boogie rock type song Frank Zappa ever did. Of course this is Frank Zappa we're talking about. Standard issue anything isn't going to be in the equation very long. Then it goes to my favorite number here,the greasy funk of \\"I'm The Slime\\",an early example of the same conceptual impulse much later expressed on [[ASIN:B00008F2SL Television the Drug of the Nation]] many years later,even down to the rapped lyrics. \\"50/50\\" comes right out at you with that exciting intersection of in the groove flamboyance of the funkier end of hard rock,and that's basically what the lyrics deal with as a character sketch as well. On the openly lustful \\"Dinah-Moe-Hum\\" it's jazz/funk/rock boogie type fusion all the way whereas \\"Zomby Woof\\" again comes at things from a more guitar oriented rockier end of fusion where Zappa himself moves up front in the musical mix.  is an alternately famous/infamous number here-a strong dynamic jazz fusion \\"Dirty Love where Zappa tells us,typically in an explicit manner of a sexual encounter involving a degree of beastiality. \\"Montana\\" ends the album on some slow and sleek bluesy funk groove.<br /><br />  In terms of both lyrics and music,whether the music be based more in jazz or rock,the key term to describe this would be as a funky album. Not only is it funky. But especially with the presence of George Duke,himself about to launch into a highly innovative solo career with Zappa producer Kerry McKnabb on the MPS label [[ASIN:B001AI1QV8 Faces in Reflection]],an album recorded around this time and more than worthwhile to pick up if your a fan of Zappa of this period,the music here is definitely based in the funk era as well. The musicians,who were of such a powerful and high quality many of them would soon become major players and innovators of their own,all dive headlong inside the groove on every one of these songs and stay right there on the one wherever Zappa's musical and lyrical conceptualizations happened to be. And even though the music often seemed very free form,it was just the charm of Zappa showing again. His music,again a good quality for funk,was so much about control and often strong perfectionism. They only want to make an \\"honest\\" living, selling their moonshine at a fair price to people in their community, but when a crooked special deputy (Guy Pearce) demands a large cut of their action, the brothers refuse and that leads to violence, torture and murder.<br /><br />Adapted for the screen by composer Nick Cave from a novel (based on fact) by Matt Bondurant, grandson of the character played in the film by LeBeouf, LAWLESS features a cast of intriguing, multi-dimensional characters, portrayed by some of the most talented actors in films today.  Jessica Chastain, as an emotionally damaged woman from Chicago who comes to work for the brothers, Mia Wasikowska, as a Mennonite girl courted by LeBeouf, and Gary Oldman, playing a big city gangster on the run, are also memorable in their roles<br /><br />Director John Hillcoat and his team have flawlessly re-created backwoods Virginia of the early 1930s.  His action sequences are well staged and riveting.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the film does have several slow spots, caused by the fact that the screenplay lacks focus.  Too much time is spent on two romantic subplots (i.e. LeBeouf/Wasikowska, Hardy/Chastain), which are, in themselves, touching, but these sequences distract from the primary storyline, the conflict between the brothers and Pearce's character.  LeBeouf serves as the narrator of the movie and has top billing, yet the filmmakers never make clear whether this is his story or Hardy's.<br /><br />Anchor Bay Entertainment has issued LAWLESS in a 3-disc (Blu-Ray/DVD/Digital) combo pack. The cinematography and choreography reflect great forethought and the musical score enhances the film quite a bit.<br /><br />We first see how Thomas Schell, a jeweler (Tom Hanks) loves to play with his son Oskar (Thomas Horn), a troubled kid who might have Asperger's Syndrome (at one point Oskar says his test results for Asperger's were inconclusive). Thomas plays with Oskar so that Oskar can build self-confidence and get over his fears which are many--including swing sets! 1935670913|2.0|First, I'll be honest: reading this book did give me a couple ideas though less for my book and more for using Twitter (I currently don't have a Twitter account but now see how it could be useful).  I can also tell he seems genuine about his audience and readers.  However, I'm glad this book was given as a gift and that I didn't purchase it myself.  Some of the criticisms:<br /><br />First, it's a very self-promotional book as many have already mentioned.  Second, I almost became sick at the number of exclamations he used.  It was easily 1 every 2 or 3 sentences, many right after another.  This just lends support to the fact that this book is more of a pitch from an actual insurance salesman than a how-to or useful book.  I believe another reviewer's analogy that it's more of an infomercial is spot on with the comments of \\"why would I give away a $10,000 idea for $4.99?!\\" where I can just hear \\"just wait, there's more!\\"  He is too busy touting his own success and what worked for him to actually break down what caused that success.  There's always a million ways to do things but if you're just giving someone 1 way and not breaking it down to the fundamentals then you're taking away their opportunity to figure out the other million and adjust it to themselves.  It's unfortunate that he was too focused on himself because if there were critical thought applied to this and targeted to his audience, as he likes to say, then it would probably be really useful.<br /><br />Of course, I have to mention what others brought up about Locke paying others to buy his books and leave positive reviews.  There was argument that commercials and actors do the same thing, but I don't think so... when you pay for positive reviews,  you eat away at the system itself which is why it is so offensive.  When we see a commercial we know what it is and what it's for, we know they're selling a product and we don't start questioning marketing and commercials themselves.  When you start being so shady as to pay for positive reviews, we then naturally question all other reviews, thus invalidating the usefulness of the review system itself.  His use of that tactic and his refusal to put it in this book also makes one question all his other ideas.  If he approached it as a whole system and actually judged what parts brought him success that'd be one thing, but now we're left wondering how much success came from fake reviews and how much came from the ideas he hawked in the book itself.<br /><br />Lastly, his book is only aimed at authors that care more about sales than anything else.  He talks about the authors that want to create something meaningful and wasn't too dismissive of them/us, but he is only talking to those authors that would write only for sales.  So as he said, this may work for you, but for a lot of writers, it won't.<br /><br />So, overall, the book is very \\"meh.\\"  It had some ideas that made me think but then again I wasn't into Twitter before.  So take it for what it's worth.  It's at least a quick read... good luck on your writing.

B004H1YH66|5.0|I went into the Raine re-recording with high hopes and an open mind, especially when I discovered that the Poledouris family was on-board with the Raine project.<br /><br />The short of it? This new production will not replace your original Poledouris recordings. Never. But Nic Raine's \\"Conan the Barbarian\\" ranks among the top ten, maybe top five, albums that I own. The conductor, orchestra, chorus, and recording are amazing. No, Raine is not Poledouris, but he and the Prague musicians may be as close as we'll ever get to the late maestro. Listening to some of the classic tracks, I felt the same thrill as when I was a teenager listening to the original score for the first time on stereo. Then there are the wonderful tracks we *never* got to hear, except on terrible bootlegs. Now we have everything we ever wanted, if not, sadly, from Poledouris himself, then from a conductor, orchestra, and chorus who do stellar service to the music. Great recording, great musicianship, great direction.<br /><br />That said, I should refer readers to F. Dean's thorough, perhaps definitive, review of the Raine recording. I concur with much of Dean's criticism, though not as strenuously. Again, the Raine recording is NOT the Poledouris version. Yes, Raine does an amazing job, and he channels Poledouris far better than you'd imagine from reading Dean's review. Raine does especially well with expansive, flowing pieces like \\"Wifeing,\\" \\"The Leaving/The Search,\\" and \\"The Orgy.\\" And he does well with the adrenalized pieces, too: you'll hear orchestral parts you may never have heard before. BUT--BUT--it's on these pieces that I most agree with Dean. The edge on \\"Anvil of Crom\\" and \\"Battle of the Mounds/Death of Rexor\\" is still sharp, but it's not vorpal-edge sharp like it is on the Poledouris recording. Poledouris and his musicians sounds like they're playing and singing for their very lives; they attack their music with Cimmerian fury. Raine and his musicians attack the hardcore pieces withprofessional gusto, but not quite with Cimmerian fury. The chorus, in particular, does not sing with the hair-raising passion of the Poledouris recording; the chorus sings beautifully, especially on the less violent pieces, but they seem unable to muster battle-lust when the songs call for it. Perhaps if Raine and his musicians had been under as intense pressure as Poledouris was, perhaps if they'd played to-the-movie rather than following the score freely, we'd have ended up with more Sturm und Drang.<br /><br />However, I do not mean to unfairly compare this amazing re-recording to the inimitable original. That would be a disservice to Raine and his musicians. Classic recordings are great, but music is meant to live, generation after generation, on the lips and fingertips of new musicians. And live it does, with Raine and the Prague musicians. It doesn't live quite the same way as it does under Poledouris's direction, but it's very, very close, and beautifully so.<br /><br />I've spent all weekend listening to the Raine CDs beginning-to-end. B006VKKAWQ|5.0|This set is a staggering value.  If your previous experiences with Toscanini recordings have been sonically painful and unhappy ones, as were some of mine, this set goes very far toward correcting a sorry record of sloppiness and neglect.  Performances that used to sound like they were the product of a miserable band of fiddlers locked in a tiny room with a furious old man now sound open and spacious. Recordings that seemed more static than music are musical.  In addition to poor sound, Toscanini has often been identified with rigidly fast tempi.  This set will let you hear how warm and musical the NBC Symphony could be--for example on the Debussy disc--and how the conductor's performances, while always taut and energetic, could be flexible, yielding, and even gentle--the final minute or two of the Philadelphia Orchestra version of Berlioz's Queen Mab Scherzo is a perfect example of the latter, where the mad rush of the coda is preceded by quiet, thoughtful and unhurried music making.  Of course, no one can restore sound that wasn't captured.  You won't mistake anything here for a modern digital recording.  But the sound here is consistently decent mono from the 'forties and 'fifties.  I am still working through the set, and I'm sure there will be some disappointments, but there have been none so far--only the joy of listening to the music making of one of the finest and most honest musicians of our times.  If you love great performances of orchestral music, do not hesitate to purchase this set.

B000MGQBQE|5.0|For those not already familiar with the play, it is the only one of Shakespeare plays without a recognizable source for the main plot, although there is documentation for many details in the voyage literature of the late sixteenth and early seventeenth century, especially the earlier years of the Virginia colony. A few hints may have come from histories of Italy, but the names don't match up with any specific events. Most of the other parallels to the plot which have been identified are too general to tie directly to the play, although they may be helpful in understanding it.<br /><br />The grumpy magician, his beautiful daughter, the handsome young hero, and the magician's attendant creatures, are commonplaces of traditional fairytales and medieval and renaissance romances. (Not to mention a lot of modern genre fantasy, and older science fiction.) So, too, are wicked brothers and scheming courtiers.<br /><br />In other hands, these elements could have made a rambling crowd-pleaser like the then-popular \\"Mucedorus,\\" Shakespeare, who was at home with the plots spread widely through time and space, here makes them the subject of a tightly constructed play. As has long been noted, \\"The Tempest\\" is one of the few Shakespeare plays to observe the so-called \\"classical unities\\" of (elapsed) time and a single place, in this case, a few hours on an enchanted. In this is its unlike most other Elizabethan and Jacobean \\"romance\\" plays, very much including his own earlier ventures, such as \\"Twelfth Night\\" and \\"A Winter's Tale.\\"<br /><br />\\"The Tempest\\" is one of my personal favorites in the Shakespeare canon, and it has inspired a long series of pastiches, retellings, parodies and satires, adaptations, operatic adaptations, and just plain productions. (My personal pick -- a purely sentimental one -- is \\"Forbidden Planet,\\" the 1956 movie starring Walter Pidgeon, Anne Francis, and Leslie Nielsen, all upstaged by Robbie the Robot, in a double role emulating both the helpful spirit Ariel and the bumbling Caliban.)<br /><br />Anyone considering ordering THIS particular edition should be aware that it is part of the OLD \\"Pelican Shakespeare\\" series issued 1956-1967, under the General Editorship of Alfred Harbage. It was published by Penguin Books, which then used the Pelican imprint for various types of non-fiction books and editions of literature. Each volume had \\"Shakespeare and His Stage,\\" a brief essay by Harbage, and an introduction by the editor of the play. The early editions were instantly recognizable as mass-market (small) paperbacks with spines and covers mainly in pale blue. A compendium, \\"The Complete Pelican Shakespeare,\\" with revised texts, was eventually issued as a fat hardcover, and the whole series was then re-issued in individual paperbacks. In either edition, they were bare-bones packages, with a brief \\"Note on the Text\\" and unfamiliar vocabulary glossed at the foot of the page. The short introductions by the volume editors were often quite good; in the case of \\"The Tempest\\" (1959, revised 1970), it consists of eleven pages by the distinguished critic Northrop Frye, still valuable as a summary of his ideas on literary modes and genres.<br /><br />There is now a \\"Second Series\\" or NEW \\"Pelican Shakespeare,\\" under the Penguin imprint, with Stephen Orgel and A.R. Braunmuller as General Editiors, issued in the early years of the present century. It is in the larger trade paperback format now commonly used by Penguin. They otherwise retain the basic structure of Publisher's Note, the General Editors on \\"The Theatrical World\\" and \\"The Texts of Shakespeare,\\" an introduction by the volume editor, a Note on the Text,\\" and the text with vocabulary footnotes (embracing slightly more complicated issues, such as puns).<br /><br />There is yet another possible source of confusion, a completely independent \\"Penguin Shakespeare\\" series, apparently issued mainly in the U.K., and much more elaborate (closer in format to the American Signet Shakespeare and recent Folger Library editions).<br /><br />Although standard practices in editing Shakespeare changed over the almost fifty years separating the initiations of the two Pelican series, these changes are of remarkably little relevance to \\"The Tempest,\\" which appeared in the First Folio, and only the First Folio, and in a fairly clean text to boot. Major issues (outside speculations that we have a heavily revised or cut version of the play) are problems in assigning prose passages to the intended speakers, and occasional metrical passages embedded in prose passages. (These theories are in part related to whether information on the performance of the play in 1611 indicates its first production.)<br /><br />Such problems are most acute in the actual storm of the title, Act One, Scene One, in which the Master of a ship, the Boatswain, assorted members of the crew, and some fairly useless courtiers are all talking at once. As a stage direction in the Folio describes offstage cries for help, \\"a confused noise.\\" Only one personality stands out, the wise old councillor, Gonzalo, mostly for his remarkably calm preaching at fellow-courtiers and seamen alike (and so continues throughout the play).<br /><br />Here and elsewhere, Frye's text occasionally \\"corrects\\" some of the Folio's stage directions -- which are insufficient by modern standards, and often confusingly placed -- and normalizes the spelling (the Pelican practice), but is otherwise comfortingly unremarkable, with no effort to make Shakespeare say what he ought to have said, instead of what the sixteenth and seventeenth-century texts in fact say. It remains readable, and useful -- but don't think that you are getting the benefit of more recent scholarship on the play, or of, for example, a better knowledge of theatrical conditions around 1611.akespeare and recent Folger Library editions).<br /><br />Although standard practices in editing Shakespeare changed over the almost fifty years separating the initiations of the two Pelican series, these changes are of remarkably little relevance to \\"The Tempest,\\" which appeared in the First Folio, and only the First Folio, and in a fairly clean text to boot. B008RZF1UO|5.0|The departure of Roy Khan from North America's Kamelot could easily have heralded their demise. After fronting the band for over a decade - his voice integral to their signature sound and his persona a large part of their identity - the void left by Khan's vacancy was enormous. Not surprisingly however, Kamelot has never been about one man - or one man's ideas for that matter - and so they picked up the pieces, found the tremendously talented singer Tommy Karevik (Seventh Wonder) and with the help of long-time producer Sascha Paeth, they moved on. To say that Silverthorn is a triumph would be an understatement for the end result here is superior to their past two releases in every capacity. And while perhaps not as majestic as the Epica/The Black Halo tandem, Silverthorn stands alone as an excellent piece of art. And not only is this a victory on the musical side, the packaging, presentation and concept are first rate.<br /><br />The Limited Edition set comes in a nice heavy cardboard box which contains a 48 page hard bound booklet with heavy quality paper and wonderful illustrations. The book chronicles the story behind the music - a compelling tragedy about the death of a young girl and the aftermath for her twin brothers and family. The story is told in \\"first person\\" by one of the brothers as he is forced to deal with the secret behind her death and the consequences of his and his brother's ill-fated choices. Well-written, the story sets the stage for this epic musical journey - one which could easily continue on subsequent recordings. Additionally, the box set contains the original recording in a hard bound digibook (beautifully illustrated) with lyrics. There is a separate bonus disc with a full instrumental version of the release (sans main vocals only) and the bonus track \\"Grace.\\" Oddly, the background vocals/spoken parts remain on the instrumental recordings. Finally, in old school fashion, there is a poster of the band. From a graphic design standpoint the box set is another huge victory and will be a must have purchase for fans, especially since the story book is essential in order to truly appreciate the depth of the lyrical content.<br /><br />Musically, the songs are a return to the greatness fans enjoyed with Epica and The Black Halo, and to a lesser degree The Fourth Legacy and Karma - the speedy orchestral rockers (\\"Sacrimony\\" and \\"Torn\\") blended with emotive ballads (\\"Song For Jolee\\") and epic progressive compositions like the title track and \\"The Prodigal Son.\\" Stunningly, Karevik sounds just like Roy Khan. Seriously, if you didn't know that Khan had left the band, you would unlikely be able to discern the difference. It's impossible to imagine that he didn't spend countless hours perfecting even Khan's inflections. Youngblood's guitars have regained their supremacy in the mix (something absent on recent work), and Grillo continues to punch out solid rhythms on the drums. Noteworthy is some really expressive key work by Oliver Palotai, assisted by Sascha Paeth. The story references a melody that is played on the cello after each funeral, and it is fascinating to hear this motif wind itself though the album. Then, at the very end of \\"Continuum\\" - the final track - we are treated to the said haunting cello motif in solo. Nice touch. Guest vocalists Alissa White-Gluz (The Agonist), Elise Ryd (Amaranthe) and Amanda Somerville (story author and choir vocals) make valuable contributions along with a whole host of others. The organ and choral elements at the beginning of \\"The Prodigal Son\\" are deeply moving and are just one example of the gift Kamelot has for \\"painting a scene\\" within their music.<br /><br />Truly cinematic in scope, Silverthorn feels like the soundtrack to its own movie, and the way in which the story hangs - along with the absolute stellar quality of the music - this release will surely have fans begging for a sequel.box set is another huge victory and will be a must have purchase for fans, especially since the story book is essential in order to truly appreciate the depth of the lyrical content.<br /><br />Musically, the songs are a return to the greatness fans enjoyed with Epica and The Black Halo, and to a lesser degree The Fourth Legacy and Karma - the speedy orchestral rockers (\\"Sacrimony\\" and \\"Torn\\") blended with emotive ballads (\\"Song For Jolee\\") and epic progressive compositions like the title track and \\"The Prodigal Son.\\" Stunningly, Karevik sounds just like Roy Khan.
